тАШрдмрд│рд┐рддреНрдерд╛’ рдЗрддрд┐ рддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджреИрд░реНрдШрддрдорд╕рдВ рдЬрд╛рдЧрддрдореН ред рдЕрдиреНрддреНрдпреЗ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднреМ ред рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд░рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдпреЛрд░реБрдХреНрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ редред

Jamison Brereton

141
Agni
D─лrghatamas Aucathya
13 verses: jagat─л, except triс╣гс╣нubh 12тАУ13
Like the last hymn, this one is full of puzzles, and also like the last, it focuses especially on the birth and growth of the fire. The hymn begins and ends with the installation of the ritual fire (root dh─Б: 1ab, 13ab), providing a faint ring struc ture; the second mention of its installation, with the adverb pratara╠Бm тАЬfurther

forward,тАЭ suggests that it refers to the installation of the new ─Аhavan─лya fire to the east, a fire removed from the old ─Аhavan─лya at the beginning of classical ┼Ыrauta rituals.
The first few verses cryptically describe the various forms of fire (vs. 2) and their production (vss. 3тАУ4). The means of production are at first mythical or metaphori cal, but in the second half of verse 4 the more familiar ritual churning of the fire is described, followed by his growth and rapid and unpredictable movement (vss. 5тАУ8; see also vs. 1c). This type of erratic movement is iconically mirrored with extraor dinary skill by our poet D─лrghatamas, who models it with abrupt changes of tense and a deliberate disregard for the usual matching of syntax and verse structure. In our reading there are enjambments across verses in 3тАУ4, 4тАУ5, and 6тАУ7, with sentence breaks in verse-interior in 4, 5, 6тАФa very rare conjunction of syntactic anomalies. The vertiginous effect of piling clause upon clause and image upon image is espe cially marked in the sequence beginning with 6b and lasting through 7тАФgiving us a faint whiff of the Gerard Manley Hopkins of тАЬThe Windhover,тАЭ which models a birdтАЩs flight with verbal means.
The rest of the hymn is somewhat more conventional, beginning with verse 9, where Agni is addressed for the first time in the 2nd person. Until then not only is the hymn couched entirely in the 3rd person, but the word agn├н is entirely absent, either as the name of the god or as a designation of the natural substance fire. Verses 9тАУ10 describe AgniтАЩs contributions to the welfare of both men and gods, while verses 12тАУ13 express hopes for further help and summarize the hymn itself. But even here, in verse 11 the poet plots a meandering syntactic and conceptual course starting from the тАЬgood fortuneтАЭ (bh├бga) desired to be acquired in 10d and amplified in the first half of verse 11 to a pun on the godтАЩs name Bhaga, with a rich set of images, a clashing set of objects to the verb тАЬhold fast,тАЭ and a covert syntactic transformation of that very verb at the end of the verse.
All in all, a tour de force of virtuosity.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Agni See published introduction. for discussion of enjambement and other special effects in this hymn.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬVerily, that visible radiance of the divine (Agni) has been so apprehended (by all, that it may be) for (the support of) the body, for which end it has been genitive rated by (bodily) strength; and that my mind may apprehend and apply (that radiance), they address the sacred prayers associated with oblations (to Agni).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Tejormey─л v─Бk: Ch─Бndogya Upaniс╣гad 6.5.4)

Jamison Brereton

Yes, indeed! It is just so: the luster of the god, lovely to see, has been installed for wonder, after he was born of strength.
When he zigzags up to it, our thought goes straight to success. Flowing together, the streams of truth have led (him).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Most tr. take the subj. of ├║pa hvarate to be the same as that of s─Б╠Бdhate, namely the thought (mat├нс╕е), and therefore must take the subord. cl. as concessive (more or less тАЬeven if / although it moves crookedly, it goes straight тАжтАЭ). However, I take Agni as the subj. of ├║pa hvarate, which expresses the usual crooked motion of fire, and the ─лm in this clause as standing for mat├нс╕е, the subj. of the main clause and the goal of ├║pa hvarate. (─лm and s─лm almost always have real accusative reference; see Jamison 2002, Fs. Cardona, and ─лm in 3a and 3c below.) The verbs do of course contrast – the zigzaging motion of the fire as opposed to the straight path of the poetic thought – but this is the result of the different natures of their two subjects, which are acting in tandem for the success of the sacrifice. That hv─Бr├б- is used of Agni in 7b supports taking him as subj. of hv├бrate here. However, see comment in

Griffith

YEA, verily, the fair effulgence of the God for glory was established, since he sprang from strength.
When he inclines thereto successful is the hymn: the songs of sacrifice have brought him as they flow

Lo, that beautiful splendour of the god, when he was born of strength, has truly come to be a wondrous sight. Though he slinks away 1, the prayer goes straight to him 2. They have led forward the flowing streams of Rita.

рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFirst, he reposes (on the earth) as the digestive (faculty), the embodied, the accepter of food, the eternal secondly, (he dwells) among the seven auspicious mothers (of fertility); thirdly, the associated (regions) genitive rate him, delighting in the ten (quarters) of space, for the sake of milking this showerer (of rain).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The digestive faculty: pс╣Ыkс╣гaс╕е = anna s─Бdhaka, the perfecter or digester of food; the embodied: vapuс╕е = vapuс╣гmat, having body; ┼Ыar─лr─Бbhivс╣Ыddhihetuс╕е, the causes of the growth of the body; the seven auspicious mothers: sapta┼Ыiv─Бsu m─Бtс╣Ыс╣гu, the rains fertilizing the seven lokas, or worlds; for the sake of milking this showerer: asya vс╣Ыс╣гabhasya dohase; allusion is to the rays of the sun; agni is identified with solar fire, or the sun in heaven, or as the solar rays, which in the hot season milk the earth by the evaporation of its moisture, and then conveyed to the solar region, whence it is transferred to the clouds, and in due season descends again as rain

Jamison Brereton

Abounding in food, he lies in his own (place) as the wondrous form of nourishment; his second (wondrous form lies) here among the
mothers, sevenfold kindly.
His third (wondrous form, that) of the bull to be milked, have the young women begottenтАФhim of tenfold forethought.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse concerns the three forms of Agni, with тАЬformтАЭ expressed by neut.

v├бpuс╕е in a, which should be supplied with dvit─л╠Бyam in b and tс╣Ыt─л╠Бyam in c. (Contra Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н], who take v├бpuс╕е as an adjective and the ordinals as adverbs. Since v├бpuс╣гe is clearly nominal in 1a, an adjectival usage in the following vs. would be surprising, esp. as there are, in my opinion, no certain exx. of adjectival v├бpus-.) In a I take pс╣Ыkс╣г├бс╕е as the gen. sg. of pс╣Ы╠Бkс╣г-, rather than the nom. sg. of pс╣Ыkс╣г├б- (so Grassmann, Oldenberg [SBE], Geldner, Witzel Got┼Н) or acc. pl. of pс╣Ы╠Бkс╣г- (so Renou). It is a descriptive or qualifying gen.: the тАЬwondrous form of nourishment.тАЭ It is not entirely clear what this phrase refers to, but I would suggest that it is the plants, which are often said to contain the fire in embryonic form (thus wondrously). In this form he is тАЬabounding in foodтАЭ both because the plants feed the fire and because plants supply nourishment to the living world. Such a qualifying gen. is also found in vс╣Ыс╣гabh├бsya in c acdg. to my interpr. (but not those of others). The root noun pс╣Ы╠Бkс╣г- is probably found also in pс╣Ыkс╣г├║dh- in vs. 4 below, qualifying plants (v─лr├║dhaс╕е), which supports my interpr.

here.

The second wondrous form is the fire in the waters, which has come to be identified with Ap─Бm Nap─Бt. The тАЬsevenfold-kindly (sapt├б┼Ыiv─Бsu) mothersтАЭ must be the seven streams. The compound is oddly formed, and Grassmann, inter alia, suggests reading *sapt├б *┼Ыiv─Б╠Бsu, an unnecessary emendation, particularly if we maintain the compound reading of d├б┼Ыapramatim in d (see immed. below).

The third form of fire, presented in cd, appears to be the ritual fire produced by the kindling sticks wielded by the fingers, which are characterized, as so often, as тАЬyoung womenтАЭ (y├│с╣гaс╣Зaс╕е). The cmpd. d├б┼Ыapramatim тАШhaving ten(fold) forethoughtтАЩ suffers from the same formational oddity as sapt├б┼Ыiv─Бsu and has been even more eagerly emended to *d├б┼Ыa *pr├бmatim (see, e.g., Oldenberg, Noten, who keeps sapt├б┼Ыiv─Бsu as a cmpd but supports emending the other to two words). The d├б┼Ыa, liberated from the compound, would qualify the fingers, as often. However, in my opinion we must keep either both compounds or neither, and since the cmpds are the more difficult readings and D─лrghatamas is a tricky poet, I see no reason to emend.

Note that janayanta in b rhymes with anayanta in 1d in the same metrical position.

Griffith

Wonderful, rich in nourishment, he dwells in food; next, in the seven auspicious Mothers is his home.
Thirdly, that they might drain the treasures of the Bull, the maidens brought forth him for whom the ten provide.

Oldenberg

The powerful one 1, rich in food, the true (friend of men) has entered the wondrous (body) 2. His second (form of existence) is in the seven kind mothers 3. The ten young females 4 have brought the third (form) of this bull forth, him the guardian, in order to milk him.

Grassmann

Das Labeross wohnt bei der eigenen Gestalt, die zweite wohnt den sieben holden M├╝ttern bei, Als dritten zeugten, um zu melken diesen Stier, als den Besch├╝tzer zehn vereinte Jungfraun ihn.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs powerful priests extract by force (of prayer) this Agni from his primitive seat, (for the evolution) of his mighty form; as the wind arouses him lurking in the hiding-plural ce (of the altar), for the sake of offering oblations now as of old.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

By the force (of prayer): or by bodily strength, applied to attrition as producing fire

Jamison Brereton

When the patrons, showing mastery through their power, bring him forth from the depth, from the form of a buffalo,
when M─Бtari┼Ыvan churns him who, as from olden days, is in hiding in the mixing vessel of the honey,

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse describes several mystical and, probably, mythical productions of fire, couched in the present (clear pres. math─Бy├бti in d, which suggests that the injunc.

kr├бnta in b has the same temporal value). I do not completely understand either of the scenarios, esp. fireтАЩs hiding in the mixing vessel in cd.

GeldnerтАЩs suggestion that the first hemistich deals with Agni in the waters is supported by the parallel passages he adduces, and so it may continue the theme of 2b.

In d math─Бy├бti is entirely ambiguous between тАШchurns, rubsтАЩ (Oldenberg [SBE] тАШproduces тАж by attritionтАЩ, Geldner тАШausreibtтАЩ) and тАШstealsтАЩ (Renou, Witzel Got┼Н), and both are appropriate: тАШchurnsтАЩ would continue the theme of fire-production, but тАШstealsтАЩ would refer to M─Бtari┼ЫvanтАЩs theft of fire from heaven. No doubt both are meant, and there is both a mythical and a ritual application of the passage. Cf. I.148.1 m├бth─лt тАж m─Бtari┼Ыv─Б.

Griffith

What time from out the deep, from the Steer’s wondrous form, the Chiefs who had the power produced him with their strength;
When Matarisvan rubbed forth him who lay concealed, for mixture of the sweet drink, in the days of old.

Oldenberg

When the rulers, the liberal lords brought him forth by their power out of the depth, out of the buffalo’s shape 1, when from of old 2 at the purification of the sweet drink 3 M├вtarisvan produces the hidden one (i. e. Agni) by attritionтАФ

Geldner

Als ihn die m├дchtigen Herren von der Tiefe , von der Gestalt des B├╝ffels mit Kraft losmachten, sobald Matarisvan ihn ausreibt, der seit langem im R├╝hrgef├д├Я des S├╝├Яtranks verborgen war;

Grassmann

Wenn aus der Tiefe, aus des B├╝ffels Scheingestalt die starken F├╝rsten ihn erzeugten mit Gewalt, Und wenn vor Alters zu des Trankes Mischung ihn, der im Versteck lag, Matari├зvan rieb hervor,

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs from the excellence of the nutritious (offering) be, (Agni), is brought forth and the consumable branches rise amidst (the flames); and as both (the instrumental tutor of the rite and the priest) combine for his genitive ration, therefore has he been genitive rated, pure, youthful, and radiant.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As from the excellence: pra yat pituс╕е param─Бn-n─лyate pary─Б pс╣Ыkс╣гudho virudho daс╣Гsu rohati; pituс╕е param─Бt, from the excellence of the sacrificial or the nutriment or food;

Pituс╕е = genitive tive of pitс╣Ы, a father or progenitor, i.e., figuratively, the g─Бrhapatya agni, from which fire is taken, niyate, to the ─Бhavan─лya;

Pс╣Ыkс╣гudha = that which is to be consumed amonst the offerings, or what expects or desires to be consumed;

Virudh = shrub or creeper; fuel;

Daс╣Гsu = danteс╣гu, teeth, or flames;

─Аrohati = ─Бrohanti, the singular for the plural ral

Jamison Brereton

When he is led forth from his highest father, he mounts the
nourishment-bringing plants in the houses,
when the two [=kindling sticks] set his birth in motion. Just after that the youngest one became blazing with heat;

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. concerns the production of fire by the friction of the two kindling sticks.

His тАЬhighest fatherтАЭ (pit├║с╕е param─Б╠Бt) is probably Heaven (Dyaus Pitar), as most take it; it also contrasts with the тАЬdepthтАЭ (budhn─Б╠Бt) that is his source in 3a. The p─Бda-final p├бri is probably not to be construed with the verb (pr├б) n─лyate, though p├бri is common with тИЪn─л, but, as often, governs the abl. (pit├║с╕е param─Б╠Бt), despite the intercalation of the verb between the abl. phrase and this postposition.

The hapax pс╣Ыkс╣г├║dh- in b is variously explained. E.g., Oldenberg (Noten) suggests that it is modeled on the immediately following v─лr├║dh- and also ┼Ыur├║dh-. In the published translation I followed HumbachтАЩs explanation (Gathas [1st ed. 1958] II.28; accepted by Narten, YH p. 161), which takes -udh as a zero-grade root noun belonging to widespread PIE *тИЪuedh ╠п тАШconveyтАЩ, otherwise unattested in Indo-Aryan. But I now no longer believe that etymology (see my forthcoming art. тАЬVedic iс╣гudhy├б- and Oldenberg Avestan i┼бud-, i┼б┼лidiia-: The Aim of PraiseтАЭ), and I would now follow OldenbergтАЩs suggestion. Note the progression and phonetic play in the p─Бda: ─Б╠Бpс╣Ыkс╣гudho v─лr├║dho d├бс╣Гsu rohati. I would also slightly change the published translation from тАЬnourishmentbringingтАЭ to тАЬnourishing.тАЭ On d├бс╣Гsu see I.134.4. As noted there, I take it as a loc. pl. to the root noun d├бm- тАШhouseтАЩ (so Oldenberg [SBE], tentatively Geldner, Witzel Got┼Н), rather than as an adverbial deriv.

of тИЪdaс╣Гs тАШbe wondrousтАЩ (Grassmann, Renou). Here it presumably refers to the domestic fire established in the house(s); since words for тАШhouseтАЩ in the plural often refer to only a single domestic establishment (presumably because it is made up of several buildings), тАЬin the houseтАЭ rather than the published тАЬin the housesтАЭ is also possible.

P─Бda c contains a curiously doubled y├бd in a single clause (ubh─Б╠Бy├бd asya jan├║с╣гaс╣Г y├бd ├нnvataс╕е), which has attracted little attention. Oldenberg (SBE) notes it but makes no attempt to explain it, and otherwise the standard tr. (including mine) do not reflect or mention it. The exception is Witzel Got┼Н, who take the p─Бda as a kind of stuttering set of false starts: тАЬWenn die beiden seine Geburt – wenn (sie ├╝berhaupt) – antreiben.тАЭ This seems to be the only way to represent what the text has, since it is impossible to manufacture a separate clause dependent on the second y├бd. But since both clauses in the Witzel Got┼Н rendering share subject, object, and verb, and the adverbial addition тАЬ├╝berhauptтАЭ reflects nothing in the Skt., it may be just as well to pass over the doubling in silence, assuming that the second y├бd comes from the occasional tendency for the relatively pronoun to immediately precede a p─Бda-final verb. Cf., e.g., for this verb stem, I.55.4d kс╣г├йmeс╣Зa dh├йn─Бm magh├бv─Б y├бd ├нnvati (also V.28.2c, VIII.13.32c тАж y├бm ├нnvasi).

P─Бda d contains an augmented impf. abhavat, which contrasts with the presents n─лy├бte (a), r├│hati (b), and ├нnvataс╕е (c), esp. since it begins ─Б╠Бd ├нd тАЬjust after that,тАЭ which suggests that the past tense action of d should follow the actions of the earlier part of the verse. Most tr. (Oldenberg [SBE], Geldner, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н) take c and d together, separate from ab, which produces a jarring sequence of tense: тАЬwhen they spur on тАж, then he became тАжтАЭ I connect c rather with ab and indeed with vs. 3 and start a new syntactic sequence with 4d, which is continued by the preterital expressions ─Б╠Бd ├нd + ─Б╠Бvi┼Ыat in 5a, v├н v─Бvrdhe ╠е in 5b, and ├бruhat in 5c. Although this is not a complete solution, in that the ─Б╠Бd ├нd тАЬjust after thatтАЭ of 4d and 5a begs for a sequentially prior preterite, it keeps the disharmonious sequence of tenses from inhabiting the same sentence. This division is also compatible with the syntactic enjambement characteristic of the hymn.

Griffith

When from the Highest Father he is brought to us, amid the plants he rises hungry, wondrously.
As both together join to expedite his birth, most youthful he is born resplendent in his light.

When he is led forward from the highest father 1, he climbs up the тАж 2, the plants in his (or, in their?) houses. When 3 both (Heaven and Earth or the two Aranis?) promote his birth, then the youngest one became bright by his heat 4.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTherefore has the brilliant Agni entered the maternal (quarters of space), amidst which pure, and unharmed, he had evolved into magnitude, so that he mounted (the bushes) plural ced before him, as he had (consumed others) prior to them, and runs rapidly among the more recent and inferior branches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Just after that he entered into his mothers, within whom the blazing one (stayed) without suffering harm. He grew widely in all directions,
when he mounted the previous ones [=plants] who spurred (him) on from of old. He races down into the newer, later ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The mothers (m─Бtс╣Ы╠Д╠Бс╕е) of p─Бda a contrast with the father (pit├║с╕е) of 4a.

The standard tr. take v├н v─Бvс╣Ыdhe in b as the verb of a rel. cl. begun by y─Б╠Бsu in a.

The problem is that v─Бvс╣Ыdhe is not accented. Geldner suggests that it lacks accent because the rel. pronoun is in a different p─Бda, but this separation does not pose problems elsewhere (cf., simply within this hymn, 3ab n├нr y├бd тАж, тАж kr├бnta, 3cd y├бd тАж, тАж math─Бy├бti, 6cd тАж y├бd тАж, тАж v├йti); Oldenberg is in favor of emending to viv─Бvс╣Ыdh├й. Taking the text as given, I construe the rel. clause with y─Б╠Бsu as a nominal locational clause; similarly (but independently) Witzel Got┼Н with a different distribution of elements. It is true that there are several y─Б╠Бsu тИЪvrdh╠е passages; cf. esp. II.13.1 тАж ap├бс╕е тАж ─Б╠Бvi┼Ыad y─Б╠Бsu v├бrdhate тАЬhe [=Indra] entered the waters, within whom he grows strongтАЭ (cf. V.44.1), but I think we must take the lack of verbal accent more seriously than these few phraseological parallels.

Again, contrary to most, I attach c to ab and take d separately, on the basis of the distribution of verb tenses.

Griffith

Then also entered he the Mothers, and in them pure and uninjured he increased in magnitude.
As to the first he rose, the vigorous from of old, so now he runs among the younger lowest ones.

Oldenberg

Then he entered upon the mothers 1 in whom he the bright one grew up far and wide unimpaired 2. When he has climbed up to the former (mothers) who from of old incite (him) 3, he runs down in the younger, later (or, nearer) ones.

Geldner

Da ging er in seine M├╝tter ein, in denen der Hellstrahlende unversehrt sich weiterhin auswuchs. Wenn er in den fr├╝heren alten Pflanzen nachgewachsen ist, zieht er in die neueren, sp├дteren ein.

Da ging er in die M├╝tter ein, in welchen er, der helle, unversehrte in die Breite wuchs; Wie er zuvor in fr├╝hre, alte M├╝tter stieg, so schmiegt er sich den j├╝ngeren und sp├дtern an.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPious worshippers then adore the invoker (of the gods), for (the propitiation of) the dwellers in heaven, as (such men) adore a powerful prince, since the many-lauded, and all upholding (Agni) knows how by (holy) act and (bodily) strength to bring together the gods and their mortal worshipper for the sake of obtaining (mutual) sustenance.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

A powerful prince: bhagam = bhaga, a great prince; or, ─Аditya, or the sun

Jamison Brereton

Just after that they choose (him as) their Hotar at the rituals of daybreak. As if gorging themselves on good fortune, they steer
straight (to him),
since he, much praised, with resolve and with might always pursues the gods and the laud (of) mortals in order to suckle them,

Jamison Brereton Notes

Another instance of ─Б╠Бd ├нd, which seems, in this hymn, to mark the progress of the ritual.

With bh├бgam iva papс╣Ыc─Б╠Бn─Бsaс╕е in b compare bh├бgam тАж papс╣Ыc─Бsi in 11b. The difference of voice is significant: in 6b the mortal officiants тАЬ(en)gorge themselves (med.) with/on good fortuneтАЭ while in 11 Agni engorges (i.e., swells)(act.) good fortune for us.тАЭ The similarity of these striking expressions makes it unlikely that bh├бgam in 6b is primarily the goal/object of с╣Ы├▒jate, as Geldner, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н take it.

The phrase m├бrtaс╣Г ┼Ы├бс╣Гsam may be a de-compounded version of n├бr─Б┼Ы├бс╣Гsawith lexical substitution. Note that n├бr─Б┼Ы├бс╣Гsa- is found in the next hymn, the ─Аpr─л hymn I.142.3. See also dev─Б╠Бn─Бс╣Г ┼Ы─Б╠Бс╣Гsam in 11d of this hymn. The double object of v├йti – dev─Б╠Бn and m├бrtaс╣Г ┼Ы├бс╣Гsam – is a zeugma of sorts, made possible by the fact that тИЪv─л can take both animate and inanimate objects.

Griffith

Therefore they choose him Herald at the morning rites, pressing to him as unto Bhaga, pouring gifts,
When, much-praised, by the power and will of Gods, he goes at all times to his mortal worshipper to drink.

Oldenberg

1 Then in the strivings for the day 2 they choose him Hotri. As if to swell their good fortune they strive towards him 3, when praised by many he moves everywhere with wisdom and power to the gods and to the praise of mortals 4 for (bringing them) refreshing drink.

Geldner

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSince the adorable (Agni), impelled by the wind, spreads in various directions, like an insincere and unrestrained chatterer, (who utters indiscriminate) praises, therefore the world is assiduous in the worship of him, the consumer of all, whose way is dark, who is pure of birth and follows various paths.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like an insincere: hv─Бro na vakv─Б jaraс╣З─Б an─Бkс╣Ыtaс╕е: hv─Бraс╕е = kuс╣нila, crooked;

Vakv─Б = bahuvakt─Б, a prolific speaker;

An─Бkс╣Ыtaс╕е = unrestrained, aniv─Бritaс╕е;

Jaraс╣Зaс╕е = stutiс╕е, praises

Jamison Brereton

When he, worthy of the sacrifice, has spread out, driven by the
wind, wriggling through the old (plants?) like a twisting (snake),
unconfined
in his flightтАФ(the flight) of this burning one of black plumage and
blazing birth, whose road spreads through the airy realm.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take this entire verse as dependent on vs. 6. It is full of rare and unclear words, but the pile-up of descriptors of the violently moving fire is exhilarating.

In b hv─Бr├б- (to тИЪhvar тАШmove crookedly, twistтАЩ; cf. hv├бrate in 1c) is taken by Geldner and Renou as тАШbirdтАЩ, but I am persuaded by RothтАЩs suggestion, enshrined in Grassmann (and see Oldenberg [Noten]), that the referent is a snake – the creature of тАЬtwisting/serpentine motion.тАЭ The quality held in common between the hv─Бr├б and fire is v├бkva-, derived from the root тИЪva├▒c тАШundulate, curl, meanderтАЩ, and the image is that of fire winding its way through the dried-up plants that serve as its fuel. From this tr. it is clear that I take jar├бс╣З─Б as jar├бс╣З─Бс╕е, with the Pp., and as an acc. pl. fem. тАШold (things = plantsтАЩ). Grassmann

identifies it as an instr. sg., and this interpr. is followed by others (most recently by Witzel Got┼Н), but the sandhi situation, with -─Б before a- essentially excludes it (though see Oldenberg [Noten] who finds it barely possible).

The sense of ├бn─Бkс╣Ыta- is likewise unclear, though its formation is transparent.

The tr. of Oldenberg (SBE тАЬwhom it is not possible to drive to a placeтАЭ; sim. Noten), Geldner (тАЬohne AntriebтАЭ), Renou (тАЬsans y avoir ├йt├й pouss├йтАЭ) seem to reflect a sense of the common idiom ─Б╠БтИЪkс╣Ы тАШbring hereтАЩ extended to тАШpush/force (here)тАЩ, with the тАШhereтАЩ elided. However, in his n. 7b, Geldner adduces PB XXIII.13.4.5, which concerns wild animals that are an─Бkс╣Ыta-. Caland tr. тАШunfosteredтАЩ, but I see another possible extension of тАШbrought hereтАЩ, namely тАШkept hereтАЩ ├а тАШconfinedтАЩ, with its negative then тАШunconfinedтАЩ. This certainly fits the PB passage and also matches S─Бyaс╣ЗaтАЩs gloss aniv─Бritaс╕е (GeldnerтАЩs tr. тАШungehemmtтАЩ).

The second hemistich is entirely couched in the gen., save for the loc. p├бtman тАШflightтАЩ off which all those genitives hang. I construe p├бtman with ├бn─Бkс╣Ыtaс╕е in b.

Although тАШflightтАЩ may seem to support the тАШbirdтАЩ interpr. of hv─Бr├б- in b, note that hv─Бr├б- is in a simile syntactically independent of the rest of the sentence; moreover, D─лrghatamas hardly feels constrained to confine himself to one image at a time.

dakс╣г├║с╣гaс╕е is a pseudo-perfect-participle, like the pseudo-desiderative-adjective d├бkс╣гu- (II.4.4) to тИЪdah тАШburnтАЩ. Both are hapaxes.

On -jaс╣Гhas- see comm. ad VI.12.2 and VI.3.5.

vy├аdhvan- can contain either v├н тАШwithoutтАЩ or v├н тАШthrough, wide(ly)тАЩ (so also Oldenberg [SBE], Renou). I have opted for the latter, but others (Geldner тАШwegelosen FlugтАЩ, Witzel Got┼Н тАШWegelosenтАЩ) for the former. Either would work, though the phrase r├бja ─Б╠Бseems to me to express extent of space and to favor my interpr.

Griffith

What time the Holy One, wind-urged, hath risen up, serpent-like winding through the dry grass unrestrained,
Dust lies upon the way of him who burneth all, black-winged and pure of birth who follows sundry paths.

Oldenberg

When he has scattered himself, the worshipful one, driven by the wind, like тАж 1, with the sound (which he produces) (?), he whom it is not possible to drive to a place (like cattle): on the flight of the burning one who speeds on his black way, whose birth is bright, who strays everywhere to the atmosphere тАж 2.

Geldner

Wenn sich der Anbetungsw├╝rdige, vom Winde angefacht, wie ein Vogel flatternd ohne Antrieb ├╝ber die d├╝rren H├╢lzer ausgebreitet hat, bei des brennenden, schwarzbeschwingten, reingeborenen, wegelosen Flug in die Luft;

Grassmann

Wenn windbewegt der heil’ge sich erhoben hat, sich windend, zischend wie die Schlange, ungehemmt Auf seinem Gange, wenn er schwarzgefl├╝gelt flammt, wenn der im Licht geborne durch die L├╝fte dringt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLike a chariot drawn by ropes, Agni, set in movement by his own revolving members (his flames), proceeds to the heavens; the paths he traverses are blackened by smoke, as he consumes (the fuel), and (beasts and) birds fly from his radiance as (enemies fly from the prowess) of a hero.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Flames: angebhir aruс╣гebhiс╕е gamana┼Ы─лlair avayavair jv─Бl─Бbhiс╕е, by limbs, i.e., flames, having motion; beasts and birds: vayaс╕е gamanavantaс╕е pakс╣гimс╣Ыg─Бdayaс╕е, creatures having motion–birds, beasts and the like

Jamison Brereton

Like a driving-chariot made by dexterous (men), he speeds toward heaven with ruddy limbs.
After that these black (plumes) of his, the patrons of the burning one, retreat from his turbulent flaring, as (from that) of a champion, like birds (from that) *of the sun.

Jamison Brereton Notes

What quality of a chariot is expressed by the ppl. y─Бt├б- to тИЪy─Б тАШdriveтАЩ is unclear. Because of the phrase тАЬmade by dexterous (men),тАЭ which seems to refer to the chariot as object rather than to its current situation, I suggest that itтАЩs a particular type of chariot, perhaps one made for long journeys. But it is also possible that it refers to the current situation, in which case it could mean тАЬlike a driven chariotтАЭ (i.e., one that is speeding).

P─Бda c is full of difficulties, esp. the unaccented dakс╣гi and the semantically anomalous s┼лr├бyaс╕е тАШpatronsтАЩ. There is also the question whether the p─Бda is syntactically independent or forms a clause with d. With Geldner (but contra most other interpr.) I take cd together. Otherwise p─Бda c would be a nominal clause of some sort, but the introductory ─Б╠Бd (recalling ─Б╠Бd ├нd of 5a, 6a) seems to call for a dynamic verb.

As for the тАЬblack patronsтАЭ I take this to be, as it were, a two-part phrase: тАЬblackтАЭ first refers to the plumes of smoke, picking up kс╣Ыс╣гс╣З├бjaс╣Гhas- тАШhaving black plumageтАЩ in 7c; the clouds of smoke surrounding the fire are then implicitly likened to the sacrificial patrons who would gather around the ritual fire.

What then to do with dakс╣гi? Two main solutions are found in the lit.: it is a 2nd sg. impv. (or si-imperative) to тИЪdah тАШburnтАЩ as it is in II.1.10 (Renou), or it is a voc. of a nominal stem of unclear formation likewise built to тИЪdah (Oldenberg, Witzel Got┼Н). Geldner refuses to tr.

and AiG II.1.408 floats both possibilities. The first (impv.) has the merit of matching an actual existing form, but otherwise has little to recommend it. In particular, if it forms a parenthetical independent clause it should be accented. The second (voc.) does not create syntactic problems but leaves the question of the morphology unresolved. I do not favor either of them, because either one requires 2nd ps.

reference, which I think would violate the structure of the hymn. As noted in the published

introduction, the first 8 verses are couched entirely in the 3rd person describing the fire and entirely lack the word agn├н-; both the 2nd ps. and agn├н- are forcefully introduced at the beginning of vs. 9 (tv├бy─Б hy ├аgne), and this 2nd ps. address prevails in the next three vss. (9-11). I find it difficult to believe that the wily D─лrghatamas would spoil his schematic division by introducing a muddled 2nd person in vs. 8. Moreover, the asya in 8c surely has Agni as its referent, which should probably preclude a 2nd ps.

reference to him in the same p─Бda. Unfortunately I do not have an acceptable solution to dakс╣гi, however. With the others I take it as an unclearly formed nominal derivative of тИЪdah, but as the 1st member of a tatpuruс╣гa with s┼лr├н-, hence тАШthe patron(s) of the burning oneтАЩ, but this is a solution of desperation and carries no conviction.

The grammar of d is scarcely less contorted than that of c. The verb ─лс╣гate belongs to a clear thematic stem and should therefore of course be 3rd sg., but the apparent subject, v├бyaс╕е, is ordinarily a nom. pl. тАШbirdsтАЩ to the stem v├н-. To make the grammar work, it needs to be interpreted as a neut. s-stem collective in the nom. sg.

(тАШbird flesh, poultryтАЩ; cf. RenouтАЩs тАШla gent-ail├йeтАЩ), a formation that is found later (already AV) but not otherwise in the RV. Moreover, if p─Бda c is to be construed with d, its pl.

subj. kс╣Ыс╣гс╣З─Б╠Бsaс╕е тАж s┼лr├бyaс╕е also clashes in number with the verb ─лс╣гate. My somewhat uneasy solution to this is to assume that v├бyaс╕е here has been reinterpreted as a singular collective and, as the noun closest to the verb, has determined the number of the verb. But since v├бyaс╕е refers to the collectivity of birds, the pl. kс╣Ыс╣гс╣З─Б╠Бsaс╕е тАж s┼лr├бyaс╕е can match it in sense and therefore function as subj. of ─лс╣гate as well.

(Another possible solution is to assume that ─лс╣гate has been assimilated to the athematic formations of similar shape, ─л╠Бrte, ─л╠Бrate and, esp., the near rhyme ─л╠Бс╣гс╣нe, ─л╠Б┼Ыate, with 3rd plural in -ate. This does not seem impossible to me, esp. since their 1st sgs. in

-e would coincide.) The published translation reflects a double reading of initial ┼Ы┼л╠Бrasya тАШof a championтАЩ with partial emendation to *s┼л╠Бryasya / s┼л╠Бraс╕е тАШof the sunтАЩ in its 2nd reading. In my view, the juxtaposition across p─Бda boundary of s┼лr├бyaс╕е and ┼Ы┼л╠Бrasya was designed to bring to mind a third term, the sun, sharing its initial with s┼лr├бyah, its gen. case with ┼Ы┼л╠Бrasya, and its -┼лr- with both. Though the patrons might shrink from the attack of a champion, birds are more likely to shrink from the flaring of the sun, either retreating from its heat or avoiding flying too high and therefore too near it. This double reading helps unify the two-part NP of c, the black (plumes) = patrons, and takes us back to the flight of the bird Agni in 7cd.

Griffith

Like a swift chariot made by men who know their art, he with his red limbs lifts himself aloft to heaven.
Thy worshippers become by burning black of hue: their strength flies as before a hero’s violence.

Oldenberg

Like a chariot that goes forward, he goes to Heaven with his ruddy limbs, adorned with his locks of flames 1. Then his black (clouds of smoke), O burning one (?), the liberal ones (?) (appear) 2. The birds flee as before the fierceness of a hero 3.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBy you, Agni; Varuс╣Зa, observant of his duties and Mitra and Aryaman, bountiful divinities, are animated, so that yo have been born comprehending them all universally in all (their) functions, and encompassing (them all) as the circumference (encompasses) the spokes (of a wheel).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

By means of you, o Agni, have those rich in drops [/gifts] become exultantтАФVaruс╣Зa whose commandments are upheld, Mitra, and
AryamanтАФ
since, following them, you were born extending everywhere by your resolve, encompassing (everything) like a felly its spokes.

Jamison Brereton Notes

After the extravagances of the last few vss., this vs. brings us back to earth and opens the last section of the hymn, addressing Agni and praising his benefits.

The morphological and phraseological parallelism of vibh├║с╕е (c) and paribh┼л╠Бс╕е (d) are difficult to convey in tr. On the basis of the vi┼Ыv├бth─Б тАШeverywhereтАЩ with the former and the passages containing v├н┼Ыv─Б (тАж) paribh┼л╠Б- (I.91.19, II.24.11, III.3.10), I have supplied тАШeverythingтАЩ with the latter (so also Geldner, Witzel Got┼Н; sim. Oldenberg [SBE]).

As in I.37.9 I construe ├бnu with preceding s─лm тАЬfollowing them.тАЭ

Griffith

By thee, O Agni, Varuna who guards the Law, Mitra and Aryaman, the Bounteous, are made strong;
For, as the felly holds the spokes, thou with thy might pervading hast been born encompassing them round.

Oldenberg

Through thee indeed, O Agni, Varuna whose laws are firm, Mitra and Aryaman, the givers of good rain, are glorious, when thou the mighty one hast been born, everywhere encompassing with wisdom (all beings), as the felly encompasses the spokes of a wheel.

Geldner

Denn durch dich, Agni, haben Varuna, der Gesetzesh├╝ter, Mitra und Aryaman, die Gabensch├╢nen, Selbstvertrauen bekommen, sobald du geboren wardst, durch Umsicht allem gewachsen, wie der Radkranz die Speichen alles umschlie├Яend.

Grassmann

Dein r├╝hmt sich ja der pflichtgetreue Varuna, o Agni, und die reichen Mitra, Arjaman; Da kr├дftig du erstandest, sie mit deiner Kraft umfassend, ganz wie Speichen mit des Rades Kranz.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬMost youthful Agni, for the good of him who praises you and offers you libations, you make the precious (offering) acceptable to the gods; new-born of strength we glorify you who are to be lauded; to whom rich offerings (are to be presented); (we glorify you) in (our) hymn as (men eulogize) a powerful prince.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As men eulogize a powerful prince: bhagamiva

Jamison Brereton

You, o Agni, impel treasure and the conclave of the gods to the man who labors and presses soma, o youngest one.
Might we now acquire [/install] you anew, o young (son) of strength, like good fortune [/Bhaga] at the decisive moment, o you who have
great treasure.

Jamison Brereton Notes

dh─лmahi in d is probably has a slight double meaning: we want to acquire Agni like good fortune, but in the technical ritual sense we want to install / establish him. For the technical sense see d├бdh─Бnaс╕е in 13b.

There is also a pun on bh├бga-, both тАШgood fortuneтАЩ and the name of the god, a pun continued in the next vs. _________ 11
Geldner (also K├╝mmel 306) takes p─Бda a separately from b and supplies тАШgiveтАЩ, but this seems entirely unnecessary.

For bh├бgam тИЪpс╣Ыc, see comments ad 6b. bh├бga- also participates in a nexus with the previous verse: in 10d it appears in a simile, but here it has been promoted to the тАЬrealтАЭ object to which other entities are compared. In the first hemistich the common noun usage of the stem is dominant, but in the 2nd it is the god Bhaga.

Contrary to Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н/K├╝mmel) but with Oldenberg (SBE) and Renou, I take d├бm┼лnasam as an adj. with ray├нm rather than as an independent nominal referring to the master of the house (Geldner тАШHausgebieterтАЩ).

Note dev─Б╠Бn─Бс╣Г ┼Ы├бс╣Гsam here matching m├бrtaс╣Г ┼Ы├бс╣Гsam in 6d. As there, the object of the verb y├бmati here involves a zeugma, of animates (the races of gods and men) and the inanimate laud of the gods.

The last clausal tag in d, с╣Ыt├б ─Б╠Бca sukr├бtuс╕е could simply be taken as a nominal sentence with copula to be supplied (тАЬand he is of good resolve in truthтАЭ vel sim.).

However, I supply a passive form of тИЪyam (presumably ppl. yat├бс╕е) corresponding to the act. subj. y├бmati of c. Cf., for с╣Ыt├б ─Б╠Б, VI.7.1 r╠еt├б ─Б╠Бj─Бt├бm тАЬborn in truthтАЭ and, for yat├б- + LOC, VIII.92.7 v├н┼Ыv─Бsu g─лrс╣гv ─Б╠Бyatam тАЬheld in place amidst all your hymnsтАЭ (also V.44.9). I recognize that this extra material may be unnecessary, however. On the other hand, see comm. on I.144.3 for possible support.

Griffith

Agni, to him who toils and pours libations, thou, Most Youthful! sendest wealth and all the host of Gods.
Thee, therefore, even as Bhaga, will we set anew, young Child of Strength, most wealthy! in our battle-song.

Oldenberg

Thou, O Agni, youngest (god), furtherest treasures and (the friendship of) the gods for him who performs worship, who presses Soma. May we thus establish thee the young one, O young (son) of strength, possessor of great treasures, like the winner in a race 1.

Geldner

Du, Agni, bringst dem dienstfertigen Somapresser das Kleinod, du J├╝ngster die G├╢tterschaft. Aufs neue wollen wir dich, du junger Sohn der Kraft, zu eigen haben wie den Bhaga das Gl├╝ck im Kampfspiel, der du das gro├Яe Kleinod hast.

Grassmann

Du f├╝hrst, o Agni, dem, der eifrig Soma presst, o j├╝ngster, Reichthum und die G├╢tterschar herbei; Drum wollen wir aufs neue nun, o Sohn der Kraft, o Sch├дtzereicher, dir als Spender Preislied weihn.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рддреНрд╡рдореН рдЕрд╕реНрдореЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рд╕реБ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдердВ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рдЕрд░рдгреАрдпрдВ рджрдореВрдирд╕рдВ рджрдордиреАрдпрдореН рдЙрдкрд╛рд░реНрдЬреНрдпрдореН рее рджрдореЗрд░реВрдирд╕рд┐рдГ’ (рдЙ. рд╕реВ. рек. реирейрел ) рдЗрддрд┐ рдКрдирд╕рд┐рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ рее рд░рдпрд┐рдВ рди рдкрдкреГрдЪрд╛рд╕рд┐ рдзрдирдВ рдпрдерд╛ рд╕рдВрдкреГрдгрдХреНрд╖рд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рднрдЧрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрд░реНрднрдЬрдиреАрдпрдВ рджрдХреНрд╖рдВ рди рдЙрддреНрд╕рд╛рд╣рд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рдкреНрд░рдмреБрджреНрдзрдВ рд╡рд╛ рдзрд░реНрдгрд╕рд┐рдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдзрд╛рд░рдгрдХреБрд╢рд▓рдВ рдкреБрддреНрд░рдВ рдпрдерд╛ рдкрдкреНрд░рдЪрд╛рд╕рд┐ рд╕рдВрдкреГрдгрдХреНрд╖рд┐ рдЙрднрдпрдордкрд┐ рджрджрд╛рд╕реАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдкреГрдЪреА рд╕рдВрдкрд░реНрдХреЗ’ред рд▓реЗрдЯрд┐ рдЖрдбрд╛рдЧрдордГред тАШрдмрд╣реБрд▓рдВ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕рд┐ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдХрд░рдгрд╕реНрдп рд╢реНрд▓реБрдГ рее рдЗрджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рдкрд░реЛрдХреНрд╖реЗрдгрд╛рд╣ ред рдпрдГ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рд░рд╢реНрдореАрдБрд░рд┐рд╡ рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпрд╛рдиреН рд░рд╢реНрдореАрдиреН рдпрдерд╛ рдпрдорддрд┐ рдирд┐рдпрдордпрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рдпрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рд╕рдГ рдЙрднреЗ рдЬрдиреНрдордиреА рдЬрдирдирд╛рдзрд╛рд░рднреВрддреМ рдЙрднреМ рд▓реЛрдХреМ рдЗрд╣рд▓реЛрдХрдкрд░рд▓реЛрдХреМ рдпрдорддрд┐ рдирд┐рдпрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рд╕реБрдХреНрд░рддреБрдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирдХрд░реНрдорд╛ рдЕрдпрдореН рдЛрддреЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреАрдпрдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдирдВ рд╢рдВрд╕рдВ рд╕реНрддрд╡рдВ рдЪ рдЖ рдпрдорддрд┐ рдЖрдпрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛ рджрджрд╛рддрд┐ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдзреЗ рдкрдкреГрдЪрд╛рд╕реАрддреНрдпрдкрд┐ рдкрд░реЛрдХреНрд╖рддреНрд╡рд╛рдп рдкреНрд░рдердордкреБрд░реБрд╖рддрдпрд╛ рдпреЛрдЬреНрдпрдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIn like manner as you confer upon us riches, (so you bestow upon us) a well-disposed, docile, and energetic (son); the receptacle (of learning and other merits), one who is the performer of holy rites, Agni, who regulates as it were his own rays, (and the condition) both (his) births, (or heaven and earth), he regulates at (our) sacrifice the adoration of the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Riches: rayim na svartham bhagam dakс╣гam na dharnasim: putram, a son is added; dakс╣гam na = dakс╣гa-like, or, uts─Бhavantam, having energy;

Bhaga = sarvair bhajantyam, to be enjoyed, or approved by all;

Dharс╣Зasim = vidy─Бder dharaс╣Зa ku┼Ыalam, skilful in containing knowledge

Jamison Brereton

For us you will engorge good fortune [/Bhaga] like household wealth meant for a good purpose, like enduring skill,
([good fortune/] Bhaga) who will hold fast both races [=gods and men], like reins, (and also) the laud of gods, and (who himself), of good
resolve, (is held fast) in truth.

Griffith

Vouchsafe us riches turned to worthy ends, good luck abiding in the house, and strong capacity,
Wealth that directs both worlds as they were guiding-reins, and, very Wise, the Gods’ assent in sacrifice.

Oldenberg

Make good fortune 1 swell for us like well-employed wealth belonging to the house, and like firm ability 2тАФ(fortune) which can hold both races 3 like reins: and being full-of good-will in (the sphere of) Rita, (fill our) praise of the gods (with rich reward).

Geldner

Uns gib einen Hausgebieter, der Nutzen stiftet wie Reichtum! Mach Bhaga unser Gl├╝ck voll, da├Я es dauerhaft sei wie Daksa, die Tatkraft - einen Hausgebieter, der die beiden Geschlechter wie die Z├╝gel lenken soll, der das Lob der G├╢tter lenkt und im rechten Werke wohlberaten ist.

Grassmann

Uns schenke Schatz des Hauses, der uns Nutzen bringt, und schenk uns Gl├╝ck und T├╝chtigkeit, die dauernd bleibt, Der G├╢tter du und Menschen wie zwei Z├╝gel lenkst, und wohlgesinnt der G├╢tter Preis beim heil’gen Werk.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay he who is one with light, who has fleet horses, the invoker (of the gods), full of joy, and borne in a golden chariot, listen to us; may that irresistible, yet plural cable Agni, conduct us, by the most efficacious (means), to that desirable and accessible (heaven).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And the bright-flashing, delighting Hotar with his lively horses and gleaming chariot will hear us.
Without error Agni will lead us with the best leading to desirable safe passage, to a better state.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The acc. goals in d, v─Бm├бс╣Г suvit├бс╣Г v├бsyaс╕е, may be a triplet (with v─Бm├бm and suvit├бm separate; so Geldner, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н); it is not easy to tell and has little effect on sense.

The hapax splv. n├йс╣гatama-, to the unattested a-stem *n├йс╣гa-, is generally taken as agentive (тАШbest leader[s]тАЩ; e.g., Geldner тАЬmit den besten F├╝hrenтАЭ), but I see no reason for this. The expression seems parallel to II.23.4 sun─лt├нbhir nayasi “you guide with good guidance,” X.63.13 n├бyath─Б sun─лt├нbhiс╕е, where agentive readings are out. (Note that in both passages the abstract is in the plural, as here.) Moreover, since Agni is doing the leading, he would not need additional leaders (though Witzel Got┼Н suggest that they are the horses in p─Бda a). In any case note the ring with anayanta in 1d.

Griffith

May he, the Priest resplendent, joyful, hear us, he with the radiant car and rapid horses.
May Agni, ever wise, with best directions to bliss and highest happiness conduct us.

Oldenberg

And may the brilliant, joyful Hotri with quick horses, with a shining chariot hear us. May he, the wise Agni, lead us on the best leading (paths) to happy welfare and to bliss.

Geldner

Und es soll uns erh├╢ren der sch├╢nleuchtende mit den raschen Rossen, der wohlredende Hotri auf schimmerndem Wagen, Er f├╝hre uns mit den besten F├╝hrern, der nie irrende Agni zum Guten, zum Wohlergehen, zum Gl├╝ck.

Grassmann

Der strahlende erfreunde Priester h├╢r’ uns, dess Rosse schnell sind und dess Wagen leuchtet; Der weise Agni f├╝hr mit bester F├╝hrung zu sch├╢nem Gl├╝cke und zu h├╢chstem Gut uns.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, possessing eminent (fitness) for supreme sovereignty, has been glorified by us, with holy rites (┼Ыim─л ┼Ыaktiс╕е: Nirukta 2.1.24), and with hymns. Let all who are presen1, as well as we ourselves, enriched (by his favour), shout aloud (the praise of Agni), as (loudly as) the sun (causes) the rain-cloud (to thunder).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Agni has been praised with our energetic chants [/with his ardent flames], while being installed further forward for sovereign rule.
Both those who are our bounteous (patrons) and we (ourselves) would extend outward, as the sun (extends) beyond the mist.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The arka├нс╕е of p─Бda a can refer both to the chants of the ritual participants and to AgniтАЩs flames, though only the first sense is registered by most tr. In the second sense the instr. is not an agentive/instrumental phrase with passive ├бst─Бvi, but an instr. of accompaniment/description.

The тАЬfurther forwardтАЭ (pratar├бm) of b presumably refers to the installation of the new ─Аhavan─лya fire, carried towards the east. The d├бdh─Бnaс╕е of this p─Бda forms a ring with dh─Бyi of 1a.

In cd the mixed 3rd and 1st ps. pl. subject am─л╠Бca y├й magh├бv─Бno vay├бс╣Г ca тАЬboth those who are our bounteous (patrons) and we (ourselves)тАЭ takes a 3rd pl. verb, n├нс╣г с╣нatanyuс╕е. I take n├нс╕е with the frame (тАЬextend outwardтАЭ) and ├бti with the simile (тАЬextend beyondтАЭ).

Griffith

With hymns of might hath Agni now been lauded, advanced to height of universal kingship.
Now may these wealthy chiefs and we together spread forth as spreads the Sun above the rain-clouds.

Oldenberg

Agni has been praised with powerful 1 songs, he who has been brought forward furthermore for sovereignty. May both those our liberal lords and we ourselves spread out 2 (our power over all foes) as the sun (spreads out its light and by it destroys) the mist.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ (рд╢рд┐рдореАрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рдд рдХрд░реНрдореЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдЕрд░реНрдХреИрдГ) рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде (рдкреНрд░рддрд░рдореН) рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдмрд▓реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ рддрд░реЗрдВ рдЙрд╕ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдЧрдг рдХреЛ (рджрдзрд╛рдирдГ) рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рд╕реБрд╢реАрд▓рддрд╛ рдореЗрдВ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд┐рдд (рд╕рд╛рдореНрд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдп) рдЪрдХреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрд┐ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдп рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдЕрд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рд┐) рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рдкрд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ (рдЪ) рдФрд░ (рдпреЗ) рдЬреЛ (рдЕрдореА) рд╡реЗ (рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдГ) рдкрд░рдордкреВрдЬрд┐рдд рдзрдирдпреБрдХреНрдд рдЬрди (рд╕реБрд░рдГ) рд╕реВрд░реНрдп (рдорд┐рд╣рдореН) рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛ рдХреЛ (рди) рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдХреЛ (рдЕрддрд┐, рдирд┐, рддрддрдиреНрдпреБрдГ) рдЕрддреАрд╡ рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░реЗрдВ рдЙрд╕ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрдХреНрдд рд╕рдЬреНрдЬрди (рдЪ) (рдФрд░) рдкреАрдЫреЗ рдХрд╣реЗ рд╣реБрдП рдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХреА (рд╡рдпрдореН) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░реЗрдВ рее резрей рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреА рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХреЛ рдкрд╛рдпреЗ рд╣реБрдП рдзрд░реНрдо рд╕реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдп рдХрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрди рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рд╣реА рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдп, рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдФрд░ рдзрд░реНрдо рдХреЗ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдореЗрдВ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реИрдВ рее резрей реердЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкрд┐рдЫрд▓реЗ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди рд╣реИ, рдпрд╣ рдЬрд╛рдирдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реердпрд╣ рдПрдХрд╕реМ рдЗрдХрддрд╛рд▓реАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдирд╡рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рдкреВрд░рд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпрдГ рд╢рд┐рдореАрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рд░рд░реНрдХреИрдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд░рдВ рджрдзрд╛рдиреЛрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рд╕рд╛рдореНрд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рд┐ рдпреЗ рдЪрд╛рдореА рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдГ рд╕реВрд░реЛ рдорд┐рд╣рдиреНрдиреЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдорддрд┐рдирд┐рд╖реНрдЯрддрдиреНрдпреБрдГ рддрдВ рддрд╛рдБрд╢реНрдЪ рд╡рдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕реЗрдо рее резрей рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рд┐) рд╕реНрдпреВрдпрддреЗ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдЗрд╡ рд╕реБрд╢реАрд▓рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд┐рддрдГ (рд╢рд┐рдореАрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрдХрд░реНрдордпреБрдХреНрддреИрдГ (рдЕрд░реНрдХреИрдГ) рд╕рддреНрдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдпреИрд░реНрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣ (рд╕рд╛рдореНрд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдп) рдЪрдХреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрд┐рдиреЛ рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рдп (рдкреНрд░рддрд░рдореН) рдкреНрд░рддрд░рддрд┐ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдмрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ рдпреЗрди рддрддреН рд╕реИрдиреНрдпрдореН (рджрдзрд╛рдирдГ) (рдЕрдореА) (рдЪ) (рдпреЗ) (рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдГ) рдкрд░рдордкреВрдЬрд┐рддрдзрдирдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ (рд╡рдпрдореН) (рдЪ) (рдорд┐рд╣рдореН) рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдореН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рд╕реВрд░рдГ) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдГ (рдЕрддрд┐) (рдирд┐рдГ) (рддрддрдиреНрдпреБрдГ) рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреГрдгреАрдпреБрдГ рее резрей рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрд░реНрдпреЗ рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХреИрд░реНрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛ рдзрд░реНрдореЗрдг рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреГрдгрдиреНрддрдГ рдкреНрд░рдпрддрдиреНрддреЗ рдд рдПрд╡ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдзрд░реНрдореЛрдкрджреЗрд╢реЗ рдЪ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрдиреАрдпрд╛ рдЗрддрд┐ рее резрей реердЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрддреНрд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд░реНрддрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджреНрдпрдореН реердЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐рдВрд╢рджреБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдирд╡рдореЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдЬреА рдорд╛рдгрд╕реЗ рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдХрдбреВрди рдЪрд╛рдВрдЧрд▓реЗ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдг рдШреЗрдКрди рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рдиреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдЪрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рдЪрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрди рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдирд╛рдЪ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдп, рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╡ рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рдЪрд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдХрд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рд╕ рдиреЗрдорд╛рд╡реЗ. рее резрей рее
